Disgusting, bloody, violent, hard, gritty, showing no mercy to anyone, murderous and hope shredding... And yet, it is addictive and leaves you craving your next dose!!! I am filled with adrenaline from reading it, but there are no rainbows and comfort foods on my mind. I want some relief from the darkness and despair, but the only way to get it is by getting the next book and annihilating it - no other way!!!</span>

<div id="review_179264385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179264385" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179264385?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780575091092" href="/book/show/7670213-before-they-are-hanged">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179264385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15862156873158915996">Don’t write off the fantasy tropes <i>just</i> yet, all you unbelievers. This trilogy shows that there is still an enormous amount of life left in some of them. <br/><br/>This dark sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944073.The_Blade_Itself__The_First_Law___1_' title='The Blade Itself (The First Law, #1) by Joe Abercrombie' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Blade Itself</a> is everything I hoped it would be. I would be hard pressed to select a favourite out of the multiple plot threads featured in <i>Before They Are Hanged</i>, but I’m probably partial to the sequences featuring the Named Men. Again, there is an old school sense of wonder to this novel, despite the modern fantasy grit</span>
  <span id="freeText15862156873158915996" style="display:none">Don’t write off the fantasy tropes <i>just</i> yet, all you unbelievers. This trilogy shows that there is still an enormous amount of life left in some of them. <br /><br />This dark sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944073.The_Blade_Itself__The_First_Law___1_" title="The Blade Itself (The First Law, #1) by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blade Itself</a> is everything I hoped it would be. I would be hard pressed to select a favourite out of the multiple plot threads featured in <i>Before They Are Hanged</i>, but I’m probably partial to the sequences featuring the Named Men. Again, there is an old school sense of wonder to this novel, despite the modern fantasy grittiness. There are some nasty surprises between these pages and many issues aren’t resolved in quite the fashion that the reader might have expected, or even had hoped for. But, as Logen Ninefingers would almost certainly say: you have to be realistic about these things. A great mix of epic and heroic, fantasy-heads can do <i>far</i> worse than giving this trilogy a spin. Unless they are averse to some swearing, violence, dark humour and the occasional rather, um, unrefined and comical hop in the sack. It <i>is</i> at times an uneasy and unsettling read, yet I can’t help but feel that this is part of its charm.<br /><br />The action scenes are relentless and splendidly written, albeit somewhat gruesome on occasion. The book showcases everything from minor skirmishes to full scale pitched warfare. There is even a siege thrown in for good measure. Two wars being fought on two separate fronts inevitably equal a high body count. Abercrombie certainly appears to have a knack for this kind of thing. You’d think that the character development would suffer in all this chaos and madness. Oh, how wrong you’d be! <br /><br />As the second novel in a trilogy, this could easily be seen as a bridging work. However, I enjoyed it even more than the first. There’s certainly a lot more going on. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944073.The_Blade_Itself__The_First_Law___1_" title="The Blade Itself (The First Law, #1) by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blade Itself</a> was very good, but it didn’t really <i>go</i> anywhere and left the reader somewhat mystified as to where the story was headed. <i>Before They Are Hanged</i> rectifies this in spades, and there is a lot of progression. Here’s hoping <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944076.Last_Argument_of_Kings__The_First_Law___3_" title="Last Argument of Kings (The First Law, #3) by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">Last Argument of Kings</a> continues this run of good form and closes the trilogy in spectacular fashion. <br /><br />Capital! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15862156873158915996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review179264385">

<div id="review_1025982052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025982052" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025982052?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bro-mantic">bro-mantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=o-captain-my-captain">o-captain-my-captain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025982052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12077934515331071355"><b>4.5 <i>With Characters Like These Who Worries About the Plot</i> Stars</b> <br/><br/><b>Buddy read with <a>Athena</a>, <a>Alexa</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15573593-ashley' rel='nofollow noopener'> Ashley</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3481302' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eon</a>, <a>Anasylvia</a> and <a>Michelle</a></b><br/><br/>The Blade Itself was a complete character study without a lot of plot, Before They Are Hanged has a little more plotting involved but for me it was still all about the characters. I travelled with them, I worried for them, I hoped for the best even in the midst of the worst and at the end I’m left wondering how they will ever get out of the complete mess they are all</span>
  <span id="freeText12077934515331071355" style="display:none"><b>4.5 <i>With Characters Like These Who Worries About the Plot</i> Stars</b> <br><br><b>Buddy read with <a>Athena</a>, <a>Alexa</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15573593-ashley" rel="nofollow noopener"> Ashley</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3481302" rel="nofollow noopener">Eon</a>, <a>Anasylvia</a> and <a>Michelle</a></b><br><br>The Blade Itself was a complete character study without a lot of plot, Before They Are Hanged has a little more plotting involved but for me it was still all about the characters. I travelled with them, I worried for them, I hoped for the best even in the midst of the worst and at the end I’m left wondering how they will ever get out of the complete mess they are all in.<br><br><b>Glotka</b><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/glotkacrew_zps007a942d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409939293i/11043316._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo glotkacrew_zps007a942d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>Strange how, with time, even the most terrible suffering of others can become . . . tedious</i>
</b><br><br>Glotcka has proved again what a complex character he is. Is he the misunderstood hero or is he the villain? I’m never quite sure myself. He can torture better than anyone but still it seems that he has a conscience and I love the inner dialogue he has. I look forward to his chapters because even though in so many ways he is awful he is also extremely clever and knows the true score. He might be dead as soon as the other players in this dangerous game he is playing. If he can’t keep on the right side of the people in power he will be the body floating in the docks. So he plays his part of the game better than anyone else and proves that just because you are horribly crippled the mind is a dangerous thing and being smart will save your ass more than a solid sword arm.<br><br><b>Logen and Ferro</b> + the rest of the travelers (Bayaz, Jazel, Quai and Longfoot)<br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/LoganAndFerro_01_zpsce8bf09b.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409939293i/11043317._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo LoganAndFerro_01_zpsce8bf09b.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I ship Logen and Ferro so hard. Both are fierce warriors with horrible pasts. Again we get to see Logen and the burden he has carried by having Ninefingers as a traveler in his head. Logen is calm, smart and collected. He hands out great advice and seems like the true leader of the pack. But when 'The Bloody Nine' comes out to play no one is safe, even his allies. <br><br>Ferro, I just want to hug you, but you’d probably slit my throat if I tried. Learning about her past made me feel so much for her character. She is a feral beast to be sure but I loved the time she and Logen spent together and how close they became. <br><br>Jazel surprisingly has grown on me, all it took was a near brush with death and some real pain to make the boy grow up a bit. He might be a decent person after all and it just make me wonder what is Bayaz grooming the boy for.<br><br><b>
  <i>‘Easy, now, and listen to me. It hurts, yes. Seems like more than you can take, but it isn’t. You think you’re going to die, but you won’t. Listen to me, because I’ve been there, and I know. Each minute. Each hour. Each day, it gets better.’ </i>
</b><br><br>Bayaz is still a huge mystery to me and everyone else he is traveling with so I guess it is only fair I’m in the dark about his character as well. It seems that Quai has started to question his master a little more and the First Magi must tell stories of his past in order to convince the group that he is prepared and will not make the same mistakes again.<br><br><b>
  <i>“All the great heroes of old, you know - the great kings, the great generals - they all faced adversity from time to time.” Jezal looked up. He had almost forgotten that Bayaz was there. “Suffering is what gives a man strength, my boy, just as the steel most hammered turns out the hardest.”</i>
</b><br><br>Wow what a journey these characters had and I will say at the end of it I was beyond surprised with how it all turned out. With all they went through to get where they were going I didn’t expect the outcome and can’t wait to see what the band of brothers + Ferro will do now.<br><br><b>The Northmen and West</b><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/Northmen_02copy_zps62aad173.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409939293i/11043318._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo Northmen_02copy_zps62aad173.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The Named men from the north have found a common ally against Bethod, but the crafty king has a lot of tricks up his sleeve and things might just get a little bloody.<br> <br><b>
  <i>”It was a bad day for men, all in all, and a good one for the ground. Always the way, after a battle. Only the ground wins.”</i>
</b><br><br>I was so upset with West at the end of The Blade Itself but seeing him in his new position and having to deal with the Prince and a few other circumstances I really began to like him again. He has practically redeemed himself to me and I honestly felt extremely bad for him at one point <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br><i>She winced and stared down at the ground beside his feet. ‘I didn’t mean to . . . well. I owe you a lot, I know. It’s just that . . . you’re too angry for me. That’s all.’<br>West stared at her as she trudged off up the hill after the Northmen, hardly able to believe his ears. She was happy to bed that stinking savage, but he was too angry? It was so unfair he almost choked on his rage.</i><br><br>So no love for West yet.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But I like West and the Named men together and it seems they have a lot to teach each other.<br><br><b>The Rest of the Story</b><br><br>There was a lot going on in this and at the end of it and well to be honest, it seems hopeless for everyone. The deck is definitely stacked against them all and I’m not sure how they will win let alone survive the upcoming battles. There are so many players, old debts to be settled, new terrifying adversaries how many more will die???<br><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/hopeless_zpsa496f93f.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409939293i/11043319.png" alt=" photo hopeless_zpsa496f93f.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br>That said I still can’t wait to see how everything plays out and I am crossing my fingers and hoping that at least of few of my favorite characters, if not all, will make it out alive.<br><br>Buddy Read of the next book cannot come soon enough.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12077934515331071355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6313617523246009427">The fun continues!!!<br/><br/>I give a high rating due to its page turning storytelling, dark humour, fight/battle scenes, and characters. Especially characters! There are new interesting characters made first appearance on this book. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[For example Nicomo Cosca and Caul Shivers. You'll love Cosca although he is an unreliable drunkard.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/>But as book two of a trilogy serial, the plots are still far from finish. At least some</span>
  <span id="freeText6313617523246009427" style="display:none">The fun continues!!!<br /><br />I give a high rating due to its page turning storytelling, dark humour, fight/battle scenes, and characters. Especially characters! There are new interesting characters made first appearance on this book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For example Nicomo Cosca and Caul Shivers. They will have more important roles on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2315892.Best_Served_Cold" title="Best Served Cold by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">Best Served Cold</a>. You'll love Cosca although he is an unreliable drunkard.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />But as book two of a trilogy serial, the plots are still far from finish. At least some questions/mysteries from book one are answered on this book.</span>

<div id="review_3512131396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3512131396" />
    <a title="Klaus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83849229-klaus"><img alt="Klaus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606218156p2/83849229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3512131396?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Klaus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Klaus" href="/user/show/83849229-klaus">Klaus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/45890750-before-they-are-hanged">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83849229-klaus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83849229-klaus?shelf=abercrombie">abercrombie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83849229-klaus?shelf=grimdark">grimdark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3512131396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13062776455502294628"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509731468ra/24354234.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Shame on me. Shame on me for not joining Team Abercrombie immediately. Shame on me for rating those other books three stars. Shame on me for not liking these characters in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944073.The_Blade_Itself__The_First_Law___1_' title='The Blade Itself (The First Law, #1) by Joe Abercrombie' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Blade Itself</a> immediately. I bow to Lord Grimdark and beg his mercy. And I kiss his feet and swear to never doubt his magnificence again.</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Ferro shook her head. 'You expect too much out of life, pink.'<br/>He grinned. 'And here was me thinking you expect too little.'<br/>'Expect nothing and you won't ever be disappointed.'<br/>'Expect no</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13062776455502294628" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509731468ra/24354234.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Shame on me. Shame on me for not joining Team Abercrombie immediately. Shame on me for rating those other books three stars. Shame on me for not liking these characters in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944073.The_Blade_Itself__The_First_Law___1_" title="The Blade Itself (The First Law, #1) by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blade Itself</a> immediately. I bow to Lord Grimdark and beg his mercy. And I kiss his feet and swear to never doubt his magnificence again.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Ferro shook her head. 'You expect too much out of life, pink.'<br>He grinned. 'And here was me thinking you expect too little.'<br>'Expect nothing and you won't ever be disappointed.'<br>'Expect nothing and you'll get nothing.'</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1604418690ra/30329508.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you haven't realised yet: I'm now a steadfast follower of Joe Abercrombie and of his First Law trilogy. I <i>love</i> this grim world, this excellent writing, and these fascinating characters. I'm still not a big fan of Ferro because let's face it, she's a mad psycopath/sociopath, but everybody else has been redeemed. All the stuff I've critizised in the prequel, all that non-existent plot, all the repulsion most of these characters gave me: it's gone, and I apologize for frowning at everyone who loves these books. Because all these things now make sense, because now I, as a writer (always wanted to say that) see where Abercrombie wants to go with this one and how he builds his story. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497916551ra/23069354.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>'I don't like this,' he muttered under his breath.<br>'You think I do?' Bayaz frowned grimly over at him. 'You think any of us do? Men must sometimes do what they do not like if they are to be remembered. It is through struggle, not ease, that fame and honour are won. It is through conflict, not peace, that wealth and power are gained.'</i>
</blockquote><br><br>So. The characters. This book tells three stories: the story of how Bayaz, The First of the Magi and his Fellowship of the <s>Ring</s> Stone travel to the edge of the world, the story of how the Union fights against Bethod and his northmen (told by Dogman and West), and the story of the Union defending Dagoska against the Gurkish, told by Glokta. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1604418690ra/30329509.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>These were a sorry crowd when it came to minding the pot. Bayaz could just about get his tea boiled, and that was as far as he went. Quai could get a biscuit out of the box on a good day. Logen doubted if Luthar would even have known which way up the pot went. As for Ferro, she seemed to despise the whole notion of cooking. Logen reckoned she was used to eating her food raw. Perhaps while it was still alive.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Story number one features the most characters from the prequel: we get POVs of it from Jezal, Logen, and Ferro. As I said, I'm still not a big fan of Ferro, because reasons (come on, she's just mad and evil). I was okay with Logen in Blade Itself, while I merely thought of him as a brute - I was wrong, there's definitely more to him than a missing finger, lots of scars and violence. So thumbs up for Logen Ninefingers, and definitely thumbs up for Jezal dan Luthar: oh my, how I hated Jezal and the first book, and how expertly Abercrombie gives him his redemption arc from selfish idiot to a fascinating character. Jezal gets his Jaime Lannister story here, and I love it.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441207738ra/16078251.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>Jezal blinked at Ninefingers' broad back as he walked over to his horse. You treat folk the way you'd want to be treated. Could Jezal honestly say that he had ever done that much?</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Story number two follows the Dogman and West. Both of them have a lot of character development as well, really like what's going on there. I've critizised that they don't really add anything to the story in Blade Itself, but here their purpose and their meaning within the story get obvious. Abercrombie could've just decided to introduce them in this one, but this way they have more depth and the reader gets more attached to them, so I get why he did it the way he did it. West spends most of the book trying to save the Crown Prince's life and trying to make his incompetent fellow officers see reason, Dogman shows us the Northmen's take on the Union and their fight with Bethod.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>People of all nations, all colours, all types, united against the Gurkish, and now dying together, side by side, all equal. My heart would be warmed. If I still had one.</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512774164ra/24632289.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Glokta narrates story three on his own, because his perspective is more than enough to show us that part of the book. He is the star character of Abercrombie's trilogy, a character as unique and fascinating like few others, and he gets a lot of screen time in this one. Again, I see why Abercrombie did all of these endless torture scenes with Glokta in the prequel, I see the purpose, the preparation, and here comes a little bit of payoff in terms of that character arc as well: we witness Glokta putting that brilliant mind of his to more than the lesser tasks he had to fulfill in book one, and we see him slowly starting to act like a decent person again.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548010141ra/26947450.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And I see the plot. I see where this story goes, and why it goes there, and how it's all connected, and I like it. Oh boy, I like it a lot. The wild introduction is over, now we're in the middle of it, and each of these characters contributes something to the bigger picture which slowly evolves on the horizon. It's blessed with plot twists, hilarious scenes, and keen descriptions of this world and the people that live within it, and I can't wait to read the rest of it - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/944076.Last_Argument_of_Kings__The_First_Law___3_" title="Last Argument of Kings (The First Law, #3) by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">Last Argument of Kings</a> is already on its way and I'll read it as soon as I'm done with my reread of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>.<b> Five stars, obviously.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1604418690ra/30329511.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13062776455502294628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1874346890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874346890" />
    <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12058788-2"><img alt="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589380555p2/12058788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874346890?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" href="/user/show/12058788-2">Ɗẳɳ  2.☊</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780575091511" href="/book/show/6588187-before-they-are-hanged">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874346890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2006748742423034870">Having waited nearly two years to delve back into this series, I was a bit concerned about picking up the thread of the storyline without becoming overly confused. Surprisingly, that never proved to be much of an issue at all—a true sign of a well written tale. Another surprising revelation was that I enjoyed most all the characters this time around, which was one of my big complaints from book one. I basically hated two of the points of view in that one. Jezal was such an insufferable snob, but</span>
  <span id="freeText2006748742423034870" style="display:none">Having waited nearly two years to delve back into this series, I was a bit concerned about picking up the thread of the storyline without becoming overly confused. Surprisingly, that never proved to be much of an issue at all—a true sign of a well written tale. Another surprising revelation was that I enjoyed most all the characters this time around, which was one of my big complaints from book one. I basically hated two of the points of view in that one. Jezal was such an insufferable snob, but nothing that a little smack in the mouth couldn’t fix. Both he and Glokta became much more sympathetic characters over this leg of the journey. However, I was still aggravated with Glokta’s constant bellyaching—I get it, you’re crippled, your body is wrecked in a thousand unspeakable ways, every movement is pure torture, but can you, for the love of God, man, give it a rest already! Thankfully, it was toned down somewhat from book one, which was torturous to read at times.<br /><br />The story picks up right where book one left off, and soon finds the cast split into three main groups. The core group of Bayaz, Logen, Ferro, and Jezal is led by a navigator to the edge of the known world on a quest to acquire an ancient weapon capable of destroying the Gurkish emperor—a powerful magi at odds with Bayaz. Meanwhile, Glokta is tasked with an impossible mission of not only holding the port city of Dagoska, which is currently under siege, but also rooting out any Gurkish sympathizers within the high council. Then lastly, Jezal’s old friend Colonel West welcomes Logen’s pack of barbarians (whom Logen still believes to be dead) into the ranks of the Union army to scout out a way to defeat the Northern savages . . .<br /><br />The story was told, once again, through the multiple points of views. Although, the author adapted a technique that I wish all writers would follow: Whenever the action perked up, he stayed with that particular POV until the scene reached its natural conclusion, rather than building to some cliffhanger only to jump to another storyline. That’s a cheap and vastly overused ploy to make a story appear to be more compelling than it actually is. I always hate to be manipulated in such a manner.<br /><br />Often, the second novel in a trilogy is a lesser work, typically populated with backstories and filler material to set the stage for the finale—not so here. This book, in my opinion, was superior to book one in every conceivable way. Not to mention, the ending to one of the POVs was such a lark that I felt compelled to say, kudos to Mr. Abercrombie for having the cajones to pull that rug out from under us. I found it oddly hilarious. <br /><br /><b>Bottom line:</b> There are so many threads left dangling here that it just begs you to jump right into the third and final book, but since I’ve already managed to hold out for two years between reading books one and two, I think I can resist the urge to wrap things just a tad bit longer. After all, my TBR pile is not getting any smaller. <br /><br /><b>Bonus:</b> In the mist of all this killing and savagery two of my favorite character managed to hook up, in one of the most awkward sex scenes I’ve ever had the pleasure of reading: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JIrm0dHbCDU">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JIrm0...</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863737483" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of book one</a>, wherein I ramble for way too long over matters entirely unrelated to the story. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2006748742423034870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_198558650" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198558650" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198558650?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198558650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17159151570719056516">"Anyone can face ease and success with confidence. It is the way we face trouble and misfortune that defines us." <br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed this book. BTAH continues to follow the troop of reluctant heroes, including Ninefingers, Jezel, Bayaz and Ferro; Inquisitor Glokta, defending a besieged city and hunting for a traitor; and Colonel West working to defend Angland against the Northman, along with a small band of Northmen with grudges of their own. In that sense, it's very much the second book in a </span>
  <span id="freeText17159151570719056516" style="display:none">"Anyone can face ease and success with confidence. It is the way we face trouble and misfortune that defines us." <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this book. BTAH continues to follow the troop of reluctant heroes, including Ninefingers, Jezel, Bayaz and Ferro; Inquisitor Glokta, defending a besieged city and hunting for a traitor; and Colonel West working to defend Angland against the Northman, along with a small band of Northmen with grudges of their own. In that sense, it's very much the second book in a trilogy, and I don't think it would stand as well read on its own or out of order. However, there is largely a complete story arc for each of our groups, so while the larger issues of the invasions and political maneuvering continue to grow in complexity, I didn't feel as if it was a complete cliffhanger ending. <br /><br />I can't say enough about how well Abercrombie writes characters. They all feel so real, layered, and different. When plugged into a quest plot, there is a risk of them turning into stereotypes, but that is adroitly avoided by the depth and feeling given to them. It's interesting that we get the inner thoughts of our select few characters, but then leaving some such as Quai or Baya, devoid of any hints except through actions or the interpretations of others. It creates tension during the quest, as Quai almost seems to be baiting the mages and more of Bayaz' role in creating the conflict becomes apparent.<br /><br />Plotwise, the quest of the troop seemed unremarkable enough in the epic fantasy tradition--the questers entering the dead city flashed on several scenes from Terry Brooks and David Eddings--but it was still well done. Using the guise of telling stories while they journeyed, the questers and the readers are familiarized with the mythical back-story to the quest. It works well, maintaining interest in the background while avoiding the info-dump syndrome. The siege itself is not particularly unusual either, but is gritty, and the process of Glokta shoring defense of the city while rooting out the traitor is interesting and full of tension. Letter updates between Glokta and the Arch Lector are an interesting way of updating the story.<br /><br />The tale is full of detailed fight scenes. If that's your taste, you'll have all the more reason to love it, but if its not, don't let it put you off, as there is so much more worth reading. One quibble is the author's tendency to use both first and last names of a character, even within the same scene, which leads to unnecessary name confusion. Small complaints, however.<br /><br />I find this series engrossing, and am glad I have the next book ready to go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17159151570719056516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer12701861865675832723">Arguably even better than the previous instalment, <i>Before They Are Hanged</i> is another suspenseful, action-packed, intrigue-filled piece of entertainment. This is far from high-level literature, but it's a damn good fantasy series.<br/><br/>Inquisitor Glokta's difficulties practically ruling a besieged city, the woes of good old West in saving a military campaign from a spectacularly incompetent commander, and our dear party of adventurers venturing forth into the ruins of the Old Empire to dig up some forg</span>
  <span id="freeText12701861865675832723" style="display:none">Arguably even better than the previous instalment, <i>Before They Are Hanged</i> is another suspenseful, action-packed, intrigue-filled piece of entertainment. This is far from high-level literature, but it's a damn good fantasy series.<br /><br />Inquisitor Glokta's difficulties practically ruling a besieged city, the woes of good old West in saving a military campaign from a spectacularly incompetent commander, and our dear party of adventurers venturing forth into the ruins of the Old Empire to dig up some forgotten mysteries - all compelling stories setting up everything wonderfully for a grand finale.</span>

<div id="review_2920074158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2920074158" />
    <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis"><img alt="Joey Woolfardis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490696206p2/4639825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2920074158?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey Woolfardis" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis">Joey Woolfardis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/45890750-before-they-are-hanged">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=ce21">ce21</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=2019">2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2920074158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12330277052434088192">I skived off work to read this. Okay, so I'm my own boss and I can afford a day off since I work every day, ten hours every day, but still. Skived off, ya hear?<br/><br/>I was a little hesitant to keep this at five stars to begin with, straight after I finished it and was basking in the afterglow but also cursing myself for not having done anything productive that day (except some admin, ugh) but I will keep it at five stars. It gave me <i>a feeling</i> which is my criteria for giving a book five stars. It's not</span>
  <span id="freeText12330277052434088192" style="display:none">I skived off work to read this. Okay, so I'm my own boss and I can afford a day off since I work every day, ten hours every day, but still. Skived off, ya hear?<br /><br />I was a little hesitant to keep this at five stars to begin with, straight after I finished it and was basking in the afterglow but also cursing myself for not having done anything productive that day (except some admin, ugh) but I will keep it at five stars. It gave me <i>a feeling</i> which is my criteria for giving a book five stars. It's not always the same <i>feeling</i> and sometimes it is as simple as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134291879?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">being the only book to ever make me cry</a>. In this case, the feeling was <b>I do not want to put this book down all of my deadlines be damned</b>. I love that feeling: that's why I read.<br /><br /><i>Before They Are Hanged</i> is the second book of the First Law Trilogy, and we are still following the same characters but their threads have weaved together nicely and the plot is beginning to thicken. I must confess I didn't recall half as much as what happened, but there were unusual memories that bubbled to the surface every now and then and I kept on guessing where we were heading.<br /><br />We are also passed between main characters really nicely: sometimes it is one chapter, sometimes it's two, but I never feel lost. Each character has their own way, their style and that really entices me. I am still in love with Sand dan Glokta and know I shouldn't be. We are starting to see each character discover their redeeming features: Luthar is becoming less of an arsehole, Ferro a little less cold, Quai a little less pathetic, Glokta a little less torturer. I like that last one less than the others, because my darling torturer is perfect the way he is, hobbling and tapping about scaring everyone, but we can't have everything.<br /><br />The political intrigue and the magical undertones are bubbling away nicely, sometimes in the background, sometimes in full view. There are clues being dropped everywhere and I find that exceptional. That is a mystery murder kind of plot device and yet it fits in perfectly here. I still cannot tell where this is going, despite having read it before. Maybe that says more than I can see, but 9 years is a long time and I could not tell you what I had for breakfast two days ago.<br /><br />And, I would like to express my gratitude and offer my applause to Joe for removing the superfluous exclaimation marks from some characters dialogue. That was the main reason the first book irked me and he has amended it very well here: still, some characters use them too much, but that fits their personality. Maybe there are still a little too many as well, but it is so much better than before that it appeases me.<br /><br />About the grimdarkness? I don't really see it. It's grim, yes. People are dying and swearing and I would say it is more realistic in some ways than a lot of battle books, but I thought that was life. To see the hope you do need to look carefully with a magnifying glass maybe, but it's there. I see nothing more than a cleverly constructed, well-written High Fantasy novel; with some clichés but also some nice twists; some darkness and some light relief; some detestable characters yet whom have hearts just as the rest of us. The serial killer brakes for the ducklings crossing the road.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12330277052434088192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer922857828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13784628992596112910">This book picks up right where the previous one left. In fact, the only reason to split this tale between two books I see was the length. There are three major plot-lines in here.<br/><br/>The first one is a defense by Union forces of its northern territory against an invasion by barbarians united by a ruthless and cunning leader. The Union has an advantage in numbers, but the majority of its soldiers are ill-equipped peasants who never wielded any weapons in their lives. The high command of Union consist</span>
  <span id="freeText13784628992596112910" style="display:none">This book picks up right where the previous one left. In fact, the only reason to split this tale between two books I see was the length. There are three major plot-lines in here.<br /><br />The first one is a defense by Union forces of its northern territory against an invasion by barbarians united by a ruthless and cunning leader. The Union has an advantage in numbers, but the majority of its soldiers are ill-equipped peasants who never wielded any weapons in their lives. The high command of Union consists of scheming politicians who do not care about the outcome of the war except to advance their own ambitions.<br /><br />The second subplot is a defense by Union forces of its southern territory against an invasion of a mighty Empire united by a ruthless and cunning leader. Did you notice a similarity with the previous one? Everything I mentioned regarding north can be said about south as well.<br /><br />The last subplot is a quest for an artifact by an extremely diverse group of people. This reminds of The Lord of the Rings somewhat, but the outcome of the quest is quite different.<br /><br />Usually the middle book of the trilogy is the least exciting one of it. In this case the author cheated to avoid this: I already mentioned before that the first book feels like a giant prolog, so the second book is the place where things started getting interesting. Most of the characters are very memorable and feel like living people with seemingly bad guys showing traces of humanity and good guys developing their dark sides. The writing quality remains very good and for the most part the book does not disappoint.<br /><br />I still find some kind of exciting is missing - I cannot even name it exactly and this is the reason for the book losing 1/2 of the star from perfect 5 star rating. Thus the final rating is <b>4.5 stars</b>.<br /><br />This review is a copy/paste of my BookLikes one: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gene.booklikes.com/post/875944/this-novel-does-not-suffer-from-the-middle-book-of-a-trilogy-syndrome">http://gene.booklikes.com/post/875944...</a></span>

His characters are what makes the book so enjoyable, with lots of funny/cynical moments. A few times while reading the book I just felt like saying “haha, I like this character, he/ she is super- awesome”.   <span id="freeText17229067366295308429" style="display:none">Joe really shines when it comes to his characters, his writing and his style. His characters are what makes the book so enjoyable, with lots of funny/cynical moments. A few times while reading the book I just felt like saying “haha, I like this character, he/ she is super- awesome”. Joe’s style is unique, and that’s what I like in his books, he can write a great book without pulling off lots of sophisticated tricks (plot-wise).<br /><br />There’s more plot here in comparison to the first book (the first 30% was another exposition, though), and the book has a great ending, while Joe pulled-off an Abercrombie-trick from his hat (which is not the Butcher/Sanderson-trick), and with a moving scene afterwards. But still, it’s a four-stars plot, so that’s why I reduced half a star from the overall rating.<br /><br />4.5/5.</span>

<div id="review_9284251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9284251" />
    <a title="Joshua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/628070-joshua"><img alt="Joshua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195517556p2/628070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9284251?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/628070-joshua">Joshua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone waiting for &quot;Dance of Dragons&quot;</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9284251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2136323570192745761">Say one thing for Joe Abercrombie, say that he's a hell of a writer. With this, he proves that he earned his status as a Named Man of fantasy. <br/><br/>This picks up where "TBI" left off, and carries the characters and plot away in new and unpredictable directions. There's political intrigue, betrayal, torture, fights galore, broken hearts and twisted limbs, love, sex, laughs, and going back to the mud. I don't want to give anything away, so I'll refrain from talking about the travails of Collem West in </span>
  <span id="freeText2136323570192745761" style="display:none">Say one thing for Joe Abercrombie, say that he's a hell of a writer. With this, he proves that he earned his status as a Named Man of fantasy. <br /><br />This picks up where "TBI" left off, and carries the characters and plot away in new and unpredictable directions. There's political intrigue, betrayal, torture, fights galore, broken hearts and twisted limbs, love, sex, laughs, and going back to the mud. I don't want to give anything away, so I'll refrain from talking about the travails of Collem West in Angland, of the Dogman and the rest of Ninefingers' old crew, of Glokta in a no-win situation on the edge of the Gurkish Empire, and of Logen and Bayaz's group on a journey to the End of the World. <br /><br />Once again, Abercrombie deftly uses the tropes of heroic fiction in ways both satisfying and surprising. The fight scenes are top-notch, approaching the Bernard Cornwell-level of excellence. Abercrombie keeps the story moving, but it is driven by the characters. He never falls victim to the fantasy trap of privileging world-building over character and plot, or of using made-up words when perfectly good English ones will do (Stephen Erikson, I'm looking at you!). I learned more about the social structure of the Union and the North, but it was through the characters and not through needless exposition. The violent meritocracy of the North is contrasted with the rigid class stratification of the Union, with serious results. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2136323570192745761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>'We should forgive our<br/> enemies, but not before<br/> they are hanged.'<br/>Heinrich Heine</i>
</b><br/><br/>Sadly I didn’t enjoy this as much as I did the first book, not that it wasn’t good but I felt as if it was missing something vital. <br/><br/><u>World building and Writing</u><br/>The author didn’t disappoint in this aspect, the world building is superb. Same goes for the writing, third person multiple POV.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>'The failure of something great is never a simple matter, but, where there is success and glory, there must also be failure and s</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText2673164597873465188" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>'We should forgive our<br /> enemies, but not before<br /> they are hanged.'<br />Heinrich Heine</i>
</b><br /><br />Sadly I didn’t enjoy this as much as I did the first book, not that it wasn’t good but I felt as if it was missing something vital. <br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />The author didn’t disappoint in this aspect, the world building is superb. Same goes for the writing, third person multiple POV.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>'The failure of something great is never a simple matter, but, where there is success and glory, there must also be failure and shame. Where there are both, jealousies must simmer. Envy and pride led by slow degrees to squabbles, then to feuds, then to wars.</i>
</b><br /><br /><u> Characters and Plot</u><br />The plot didn’t really progress much, more than half of the main characters(Logen, Jazel, Ferro, Bazel) are on a journey, it took 90% of the whole book before they reached where they were going, the whole journey was kind of boring, just few occurrences that was fun to read. And what happened when they got there was so underwhelming. There was good character development for Jezal, Logen and Ferro, I think Bazel is one dimensional, there was no progress whatsoever in his character.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>A choice between killing and dying is no choice at all. You have to be realistic about these things.</i>
</b><br /><br />It was the part of Glokta my favourite character in the series that have a major progress in the whole book, I was always glad whenever it was his POV. What I love more about Glokta is his tendency to always surprise me by doing good things. That of Collem West and the Dogman wasn’t bad either, with these two I got to know how the war was progressing.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3084313427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3084313427" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3084313427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16306694628267207988">Before They Are Hanged (The First Law #2), Joe Abercrombie<br/>Before They Are Hanged is the second novel in the First Law Trilogy. Superior Glokta has a problem. How do you defend a city surrounded by enemies and riddled with traitors, when your allies can by no means be trusted, and your predecessor vanished without a trace? It's enough to make a torturer want to run -- if he could even walk without a stick. Northmen have spilled over the border of Angland and are spreading fire and death across th</span>
  <span id="freeText16306694628267207988" style="display:none">Before They Are Hanged (The First Law #2), Joe Abercrombie<br />Before They Are Hanged is the second novel in the First Law Trilogy. Superior Glokta has a problem. How do you defend a city surrounded by enemies and riddled with traitors, when your allies can by no means be trusted, and your predecessor vanished without a trace? It's enough to make a torturer want to run -- if he could even walk without a stick. Northmen have spilled over the border of Angland and are spreading fire and death across the frozen country. Crown Prince Ladisla is poised to drive them back and win undying glory. There is only one problem -- he commands the worst-armed, worst-trained, worst-led army in the world. And Bayaz, the First of the Magi, is leading a party of bold adventurers on a perilous mission through the ruins of the past. The most hated woman in the South, the most feared man in the North, and the most selfish boy in the Union make a strange alliance, but a deadly one. They might even stand a chance of saving mankind from the Eaters -- if they didn't hate each other quite so much. Ancient secrets will be uncovered. Bloody battles will be won and lost. Bitter enemies will be forgiven -- but not before they are hanged.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهاردهم ماه دسامبر سال 2017 میلادی<br />عنوان: ‏‫پیش از آنکه به دار آویخته شوند؛ نویسنده: جو اَبرکرومبی‬؛ مترجم: سعید سیمرغ؛ تهران: کتابسرای تندیس، ‏‫1396؛ در 792 ص؛ فروست: نخستین قانون - کتاب دوم؛ شابک: 9786001822988؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده 20 م<br /><br />فرمانده «گلوکتا» مشکلی دارد. چطور باید از شهری دفاع کند، که دشمن از بیرون آن را محاصره کرده، و از درون مملو از خیانت­کاران است، آن هم زمانی که هم­پیمانان، به هیچ­وجه قابل اعتماد نیستند، و فرمانده­ی پیشین شهر هم، بدون هیچ ردی ناپدید شده است؟ همین کافی است، تا یک شکنجه­ گر را وادار به گریز کند، البته اگر بتواند بدون عصا، قدم از قدم بردارد. مردان شمالی در آنگلند پخش شده، و مشغول پراکندن آتش و مرگ، در آن سرزمین یخ زده هستند. ولیعهد «لادیسلا» آماده شده، تا آن­ها را به عقب براند، و افتخاری ابدی، برای خود به دست بیاورد. تنها مشکلی که وجود دارد، اینست که او فرماندهی لشکری را بر عهده دارد که بی­ سلاح ­ترین، بی­ تجربه ­ترین، و بی ­هدف­ترین لشکر تمام دنیاست. و بیاز، نخستین ساحران، گروهی از برجستگان و ماجراجوین را با خود به ماموریتی خطرناک، در ویرانه­ های دوران گذشته برده است. منفورترین زن سرزمین جنوبی، ترسناک­ترین مرد سرزمین شمالی و خودخواه ترین پسر سرزمین­های متحد، گروهی عجیب، ولی مرگبار هستند. آن­ها شاید این بخت را داشته باشند تا بتوانند بشریت را از بلای آدمخواران نجات دهند، البته اگر این همه از هم متنفر نباشند. رازهای باستانی آشکار خواهند شد. نبردهای خونین به پیروزی و شکست، خواهند انجامید و دشمنان دیرینه بخشوده خواهند شد، ولی نه پیش از آنکه به دار آویخته شوند...؛ نقل نمونه متن از آغاز کتاب: «بخش نخست: ما باید دشمنانمان را عفو کنیم، ولی نه پیش از آنکه به دار آویخته شوند! هاینریش هاین. : یکسان گر بزرگ: لعنت بر مه! مه وارد چشم میشود و نمیشود بیش از چند گام جلوتر را دید. وارد گوش میشود و دیگر هیچ صدایی شنیده نمیشود. اگر هم شنیده شود، نمیتوان گفت که از کدام سو میآید. وارد بینی میشود و دیگر بویی به جز بوی نم به مشام نمیرسد. لعنت بر مه! مه نفرین دیدبانها است. آنها چند روز پیش، از وایتفلو گذشته بودند، از سرزمین شمالی بیرون آمده، و وارد قلمرو آنگلند شده بودند. داگمن در تمام طول راه، نگران و عصبی بود، و در یک سرزمین غریب، و در میانه ی جنگی که ربطی به آنها نداشت، دیدبانی میداد و منطقه را شناسایی میکرد. همه ی اعضای گروه هم نگران بودند، و زود خشمگین میشدند. به جز تری تریز، هیچکدامشان تاکنون پا از سرزمین شمالی بیرون نگذاشته بودند. البته نمیتوانست در مورد هاردینگ گوشت تلخ مطمئن باشد. او هیچوقت درباره ی جاهایی که رفته بود حرف نمیزد. آنها از کنار چند مزرعه گذشتند که سوخته و خاکستر شده بود. همین طور یک دهکده ی خالی از جمعیت. دهکده ای متعلق به سرزمینهای متحد، با ساختمانهایی بزرگ و چهارگوش. ردپای مردم و اسبها را میدیدند. کلی ردپا آنجا بود، ولی از خود مردم اثری نبود. داگمن میدانست که بتهود زیاد از آنجا دور نیست، هر چند که لشکرش در آن سرزمین پراکنده شده بودند و به دنبال شهرها میگشتند تا آنها را بسوزانند، به دنبال غذا میگشتند تا بدزدند و به دنبال مردم میگشتند تا آنها را بکشند. هر جور خرابکاری که بشود تصورش را کرد. بتهود همه جا دیدبان داشت. اگر داگمن یا هرکدام از اعضای گروه به دامش میافتادند، به خاک باز میگشتند. بازگشتی که سریع و آسان نبود. داگمن شکی نداشت که تکه تکه شان میکردند و سر و بقیه ی اعضای بدنشان را روی نیزه میزدند. اگر گیر سربازان سرزمینهای متحد میافتادند هم به احتمال زیاد کشته میشدند. هرچه نباشد، جنگ در جریان بود و موقع جنگ کسی نمیتوانست درست فکر کند. داگمن اصلاً انتظار نداشت که آنها وقت تلف کنند تا بین شمالیهای دوست و شمالیهای دشمن فرق بگذارند. زندگی چیزی نیست به جز جنگ با خطرات. همین کافی است تا هر کسی را نگران کند و او هم بیشتر وقتها نگران بود و حالا این مه که قوز بالای قوز شده بود. این همه چهار دست و پا خزیدن در آن فضای تیره و تار او را تشنه کرده بود. پس از میان بوته ای که میانش پنهان شده بود بیرون آمد و به سوی جایی رفت که میتوانست صدای شرشر آب رودخانه ای را بشنود. کنار رودخانه زانو زد. ساحل رودخانه گل آلود و پر از برگهای در حال پوسیدن بود، ولی داگمن فکر نمیکرد که یک خرده گل، فرقی به حالش داشته باشد. دیگر امکان نداشت که از این کثیفتر شود. دستش را در رودخانه فروبرد و یک مشت آب برداشت و نوشید. نزدیک رودخانه نسیم ملایمی میوزید و مه را هر از گاهی به اینسو و آنسو میراند. همین موقع بود که داگمن آن مرد را دید. او درست جلوی داگمن دراز کشیده بود. پاهایش درون رودخانه بودند و بالا تنه اش روی ساحل بود. آن دو چند لحظه به یکدیگر خیره شدند و هر دو کاملاً غافلگیر شده بودند. چوب درازی از پشت مرد بیرون زده بود. یک نیزه ی شکسته بود. تازه آنموقع بود که داگمن فهمید دارد به یک مرد مرده نگاه میکند. آب را تف کرد و چهار دست و پا دور شد. به دقت دور و برش را بررسی میکرد تا مطمئن شود کسی منتظرش نیست که شمشیرش را در پشت او فرو کند. جسد متعلق به مردی بود حدوداً بیست و چهار پنج ساله، با موهای زرد که خون قهوه ای روی لبهای رنگ پریده اش خشک شده بود. یک ژاکت نمدی به تن داشت که در اثر رطوبت باد کرده بود. از همانها که زیر جوشن میپوشند. پس یک جنگجو بود؛ سربازی که شاید از لشکرش جدا افتاده و کشته شده بود. بی شک یکی از سربازان سرزمینهای متحد بود، ولی اکنون که آنجا افتاده و مرده بود، از نظر داگمن هیچ فرقی با بقیه ی مرده ها نداشت. همه ی مرده ها مانند هم بودند. داگمن زیر لب به خود گفت: «یکسان گر بزرگ!» مردم کوه نشین این لقب را به مرگ داده بودند. چون همه ی تفاوتها را از میان میبرد. تفاوت بین مردان نام آور و آنها که کسی نبودند، خواه جنوبی باشند یا شمالی. همه در آخر گیر مرگ میافتادند و او با همه یکسان رفتار میکرد. این یکی انگار همین یکی دو روز پیش مرده بود. معنی اش این بود که کسی که او را کشته، شاید همین نزدیکیها باشد. داگمن نگران شد. به نظرش میرسید که مه پر از صداهای عجیب و غریب شده است. شاید صد نفر قلچماق خارج از دیدرس منتظرش ایستاده باشند. شاید هم هیچ کسی آنجا نبود و آن صدا هم صدای آب رودخانه بود که در بسترش حرکت میکرد. جسد را همانجا رها کرد و دزدانه به سوی درختان رفت. از پشت تنه ی یک درخت، به پشت دیگری میپرید و درختانی که پشت سر میگذاشت، میان مه محو میشدند. پایش به جسد دیگری گیر کرد و سکندری خورد. جسد تا نیمه زیر توده ای از برگها دفن شده بود. به پشت افتاده و دستانش از هم باز شده بودند. سپس از کنار جسد دیگری گذشت که به زانو نشسته بود و چند تیر هم به پهلویش فرو رفته بود. صورت جسد روی زمین و ماتحتش در هوا بود. حقیقت این بود که هیچکس نمیتوانست به هنگام مرگ وقارش را حفظ کند. داگمن سرعتش را بیشتر کرد. مشتاق بود تا نزد بقیه برگردد و به آنها بگوید که چه دیده است. مشتاق بود تا هرچه زودتر از آن اجساد دور شود. اگرچه تا کنون جسدهای زیادی دیده بود، ولی باز هم از اینکه در میان مرده ها باشد احساس ناراحتی میکرد. تبدیل کردن انسان به یک لاشه کار آسانی بود. خودش هزار راه برای اینکار بلد بود. ولی وقتیکه آنکار انجام میشد، دیگر بازگشتی در کار نبود. یک لحظه، یک انسان آنجا ایستاده بود، پر از امید، اندیشه و آرزو. انسانی که دوستانی داشت و خانواده ای و جایی که از آنجا آمده بود. لحظه ی بعد تبدیل به یک مرده شده بود. این چیزها داگمن را به یاد مخمصه هایی انداخت که در آنها گرفتار شده بود، نبردها و جنگهایی که در آنها شرکت داشت. به این اندیشید که خوش اقبال بوده که هنوز میتواند نفس بکشد. خیلی خوش اقبال و به این اندیشید که شاید اقبالش دیگر دوام نیاورد. حالا تقریباً میدوید. حواسش پرت شده بود؛ مانند یک پسر بچه ی بی تجربه، با بیفکری در میان مه میدوید. نه به زمانی که در اختیار داشت فکر میکرد، نه هوا را بو میکشید، نه گوش میسپرد. مرد نام آوری مانند او، کسی که در تمام سرزمین شمالی دیدبانی داده بود، باید بهتر از اینها رفتار میکرد. ولی او که نمیتوانست همیشه گوش به زنگ باشد. به خاطر همین، چیزی را که نزدیک میشد، ندید. چیزی محکم به پهلویش خورد و او را به زمین انداخت. به حالت چهار دست و پا درآمد، ولی یک نفر با لگد او را روی زمین انداخت؛ داگمن تقلا کرد، ولی این بی پدر و مادر، هر که بود، زورش خیلی زیاد بود. پیش از اینکه بفهمد، روی زمین پهن شده بود و مقصر هم خودش بود. خودش و البته آن جسدهای درون مه. دستی دور گلویش پیچید و شروع به فشردن خرخره اش کرد. گفت: «آخخخ!» دستش را دور آن دست پیچید و به این اندیشید که لحظه ی آخر عمرش فرا رسیده. به این فکر کرد که باید همه ی آرزوهایش را به گور ببرد. یکسان گر بزرگ حالا رو به سوی او کرده بود... ؛سپس دستی که گلویش را گرفته بود، فشردن را متوقف کرد. کسی در گوشش گفت: «داگمن، تویی؟» «آآآی!» دست از دور گلویش باز شد و او به شدت نفس نفس زد. احساس کرد کسی یقه اش را گرفت و بالا کشید. «خاک بر سرت، داگمن! نزدیک بود بکشمت!» داگمن آن صدا را به خوبی میشناخت. صدای آن بلک داو حرامزاده بود. کمی خشمگین بود از اینکه نزدیک بود خفه شود و بمیرد و کمی هم خوشحال بود که زنده مانده بود. میتوانست صدای داو را بشنود که به او میخندید. صدای قهقهه اش مثل قارقار کلاغ بود. بلک داو گفت: «حالت خوبه؟» داگمن که هنوز نفس نفس میزد با صدای خس خسی اش گفت: «انتظار خوشامدگویی گرمتری داشتم.» «خودتو آدم خوش شانسی بدون. چون ممکن بود از این هم سردتر باشه. خیلی سردتر؛ فکر کردم یکی از دیدبانای بتهودی. فکر کردم از اون طرف، از دره اومدی.» داگمن آهسته گفت: «حالا دیدی که اینطور نیست. بقیه کجان؟» «بالای تپه، اونور این مه لعنتی. مواظب دوروبرن.» داگمن به سویی که بلک داو نشان داده بود سری تکان داد و گفت: «این اطراف یه عالمه جنازه ریخته.» بلک داو طوری که انگار فکر نمیکرد داگمن بداند «یک عالمه جنازه» چه معنی دارد. گفت: «یه عالمه جنازه؟ هه!» «آره، حداقل چندتایی بودن. فکر کنم آدمهای سرزمین متحد باشن. انگار که اینجا جنگ شده.» بلک داو دوباره خندید و گفت: «که فکر کنی جنگ ده!» داگمن نمی دانست که منظور او از این طرز حرف زدن چیست. ...)؛ پایان نقل. ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer905309523144940746"><b> Heterogeneous </b><br/>This follow-up book in the First Law trilogy has a greater adventure than the first book. The battles and fighting continue relentlessly. The sense of expanse widens even further – to the ends of the world. The characters are further developed and nothing is predictable in their personalities. The story continues at a rapid page-turning wide-eyed pace.<br/><br/>Bayaz, the First of the Magi, is leading a band of adventurers on a perilous mission to distant lands. The most hated and deadly wo</span>
  <span id="freeText905309523144940746" style="display:none"><b> Heterogeneous </b><br />This follow-up book in the First Law trilogy has a greater adventure than the first book. The battles and fighting continue relentlessly. The sense of expanse widens even further – to the ends of the world. The characters are further developed and nothing is predictable in their personalities. The story continues at a rapid page-turning wide-eyed pace.<br /><br />Bayaz, the First of the Magi, is leading a band of adventurers on a perilous mission to distant lands. The most hated and deadly woman in the South, Ferro, the most feared man in the North, Logan Ninefingers, and the most selfish boy in the Union, Jezel, make a strange alliance. Their ability to inflict brutal damage to opponents is tempered with their loyalty and sense of justice. As a band of warriors, their cohesion and diversities continue to captivate. We get to see deeper into their nature and the subtle charisma with several is surprising.<br /><br />Several other characters are so intriguing including Glokta, the Inquisitor. Having to defend his city knowing it is full of traitors that he must root out, where no-one can be trusted and where failure means execution. We will have our favourites but imagine feeling empathy and fond gravitation towards an Inquisitor!<br /><br />This is an amazing fantasy adventure that is full of wonderfully drawn characters, a landscape that comes alive in the writing, and a plot that is ridiculously imaginative.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this book and the whole First Law trilogy.</span>

<div id="review_2107057548" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107057548" />
    <a title="ChopinFC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc"><img alt="ChopinFC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545283749p2/51633786.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2107057548?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
