        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107057548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3950928082991230987"><b>Full review...<br/><br/> 5 Stars<br/><br/> Abercrombie does it again! <i>Before They Are Hanged</i> is a superb follow up series with fantastic characters devious plots and schemes and volatile action that does not stop until the very end! This book is an incredible achievement for a sophomore series. </b><br/><br/>Picture you live in a world much like the medieval times, with large castles and rustic brick roads and villages, where magic both pure and innocent as well as dark and omnipotent are found in the deep confines of the world.</span>
  <span id="freeText3950928082991230987" style="display:none"><b>Full review...<br><br> 5 Stars<br><br> Abercrombie does it again! <i>Before They Are Hanged</i> is a superb follow up series with fantastic characters devious plots and schemes and volatile action that does not stop until the very end! This book is an incredible achievement for a sophomore series. </b><br><br>Picture you live in a world much like the medieval times, with large castles and rustic brick roads and villages, where magic both pure and innocent as well as dark and omnipotent are found in the deep confines of the world. Imagine the church, and it's forever dominating inquisicion forge 'truths' from torture chambers and heavy hooks and chains... where battles are inundated by the sounds of crashing swords, chinks of armor and the only sound you hear are hysterical yells of pain and the squeal of dying horses... This to me is the world of the masterpiece by Joe Abercrombie <i> Before They are Hanged </i><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509906234i/24369700._SX540_.jpg" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> Chaotic battle in 'Before They are Hanged'</i><br><br><b>It's amazing how reading can take you places you never imagine existed! </b>Joe Abercrombie's <i> The First Law series</i> completely blew me away from the get go! I didn't write a full review for the first book, but it was superbly written and developed. Abercrombie probably tops himself in this second installement of the trilogy, as we revisit the adventures and misadventures of such memorable characters! <br><br>Abercrombie has instantly become one of my favorite fantasy authors after I read the first book in this series, <i> The Blade Itself</i>. The writing is like nothing I've read before in the fantasy genre. Certainly there are many elements of 'grimdark' fantasy in the story, with lots of violence, gore and awesome battle scenes. Yet, Abercrombie can interlude such brilliant moments of innocence and grandiosity, that one would think to be reading an epic fantasy novel! <br><br><br><b> The action in 'Before They Are Hanged' is unrelenting and incredible!</b> The tension in a chapter can go from tame boring to nuclear in 2.2 seconds! Certainly that is one of the addicting qualities in his writing. In one moment a group of characters are walking along a deserted road on a sunny and tranquil day, and the next a group of 'shankas' (also known as 'flatheads') can be waiting 'round the corner for a full all out death experience! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509908820i/24369908._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> Ugly but deadly Shanka</i><br><br>The second book pics up chronologically after the end of the first book. The story is subdivided into 3 separate arcs. One follows <i>'Logen Ninefingers', captain Jazal and Bayaz</i> 'first of the Magi' ( a sort of wizardry 'Gandalf) in their quest for an evil magician. The second plot follows captain 'West' and the his battle for the troop of 'Angland' against the Northmen. <br><br>Finally the last arc is my favorite, as everything related to the devilishly fun character of <i> inquisitor Glokta.</i> A word on Abercrombie and his style of character creation: they are all unique, interesting to the core and bad asses! The dialogue between characters is ever dynamic. There are so many memorable lines, with lots of curses and grimdark themes, but never done in a distasteful way. <br><br><br>Inquisitor Glokta, oh Glokta! What a fucked up, deranged, borderline schizophrenic character who's by far my <b> FAVORITE</b> character in the whole series. To understand his present horrific shortcomings one must look at his tragic past! Glokta was a master fencer, a high captain of distinguished valor in the arm of 'Angland', before he was capture by enemy troops and tortured to smithereens. After getting tortured for months, including physical, psychological and emotional abuse, the end result is the broken Glokta... a shadow of his previous self! Boy oh boy, but he is a clusterfuck mess! <br><br> I always imagine Glokta after the character 'caliban' (from the movie 'Logan'). Glokta is bald, toothless, has ample physical deformities from his previous torture days which make him walk hunched back and limping... a true gruesome sight, specially as he is chosen as the major 'inquisitor' for the church! They say, 'to the victor goes the spoils'... in Glokta's case, to the 'tortured, goes a crazed and jaded inquisitor'.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509908820i/24369909._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> Inquisitor Glokta</i><br><br>Glokta has constant internal struggles with himself. Abercrombie masterfully crafts a character who's both sadistic, angry with the world, but clearly processes an internal struggle of identity and right vs wrong. Abercrombie describe's what Glokta is thinking (on a first POV) and immediately his response to other characters! These moments of inner struggle and the ones he's having 'fun' torturing prisoners are what make him such a fascinating character! Here's an example of his constant dialogue with himself: <br><br> " His grotesque, toeless left leg twitched to itself, still beyond his control. He glared down at it with a burning hatred. <i> Fucking horrible thing. Revolting useless lump of flesh. Why didnt' they just cut you off? Why dont I still? </i> But he knew why not...<br><br><b>Abercrombie achieves near nirvana in this incredible follow up series with <i> Before They Are Hanged </i>. Incredible characters full of tension and emotion, battle scenes of epic proportions and lots of humor and grimdark moments, make this book a must read!<br><br> 5 Stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3950928082991230987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3571161743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3571161743" />
    <a title="Dave" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35045983-dave"><img alt="Dave" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496413985p2/35045983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3571161743?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dave" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dave" href="/user/show/35045983-dave">Dave</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26248534-before-they-are-hanged">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35045983-dave?shelf=read-borrowed">read-borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35045983-dave?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35045983-dave?shelf=fantasy-epic-fantasy-high">fantasy-epic-fantasy-high</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35045983-dave?shelf=fantasy-grimdark">fantasy-grimdark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3571161743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3908274956927761847">Awesome! Following up on his opening salvo in the First Law Trilogy ("The Blade Itself"), Abercrombie has taken our crew of characters and stretched their story arcs about as far as they can bend. This grim fantasy set in a time when battle is still by sword and axe, where industrialization and modern banking has begun, and a few small pockets of magic remain. There are three parallel stories in this volume, set in the frozen north, the burning south, and in the west in a continent that once hou</span>
  <span id="freeText3908274956927761847" style="display:none">Awesome! Following up on his opening salvo in the First Law Trilogy ("The Blade Itself"), Abercrombie has taken our crew of characters and stretched their story arcs about as far as they can bend. This grim fantasy set in a time when battle is still by sword and axe, where industrialization and modern banking has begun, and a few small pockets of magic remain. There are three parallel stories in this volume, set in the frozen north, the burning south, and in the west in a continent that once housed the world's mightiest empire. In each story, we get a sense of the nobility of a certain degree of savagery contraposed against a corrupt enfeebled civilization. <br /><br />In the north, Angland is falling to Bethod and his Carls. Captain West is saddled with protecting the crown prince and his tents and courtiers. Dogman and a handful of Named men are about to show West what it means to be a true warrior. As so often happens in this series, war is hell, at least for the grim brutal men who must fight it on the ground and hope they are the ones who walk off the battlefield. Beats being buried there. Here, it is Captain West who appears to have character growth and who sees battle for what it is and the foppish nobles for what they are. There is a sharp contrast between how the nobles given ranks of generals and such act and how the five Named Men from the North act, doing what must be done. <br /><br />In the south, Inquisitor Glotka has survived his wars. That is, if being a bitter cripple is what you call surviving. He is at once the character who most readers may despise because he knowingly states he has no morals, no ethics, but self-preservation. Nevertheless, he is an absolutely fascinating character study as he plots to somehow wrest victory from certain defeat, believing that if the city falls, so does he. He has been tasked with the impossible saving an isolated outpost City against countless hordes of the Ghurka Empire. And there's no one on his side he can trust, not the merchants, not the nobles, and not the mercenaries, all for sale to the highest bidder. <br /><br />In the West, the First of the Magi leads a motley crew across a hostile continent, each necessary for a purpose, with a mission of saving the world. Here, civilized behavior is left behind and our hero from Auda, Jezal, must learn real survival skills from the Bloody Nine, a man who knows not friend from foe when he's in a killing frenzy. You get the sense here that Jezal is on the quest to learn lessons about character and what matters in life and that he will return to Auda a changed man, one who is not content to go to royal balls and banquets. Even so, the Bloody Nine and Ferro are incredible characters, complex, angry (most of the time), deeply wounded in the heart and soul, and uncompromising. At times, this journey across the western continent, crossing barrier mountains, entering forbidden cities, feels like the quest to Mordor to destroy the one ring to rule them all, but the road to Mordor was never this bloody, never this perilous, and the characters there never this grim, dark, resigned, or destructive. <br /><br />Perfectly plotted, impossible to put down, and Just plain great reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3908274956927761847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2070850634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2070850634" />
    <a title="Lema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18145934-lema"><img alt="Lema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507843225p2/18145934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2070850634?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lema" href="/user/show/18145934-lema">Lema</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26248534-before-they-are-hanged">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lema by: </span>
      Petrik Leo
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2070850634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8902219106199863123"><b>Guys! This book is so awesomely non-cliché I can't even..!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503701520ra/23687614.gif' width='480' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok, first let's put some context into why I loved this so much. So I'm working like crazy and barely have time to read more than 1 hour each day, so reading these in slow doses over 1 month has been such a treat.. I would come back every day eager to jump into my pajamas and spend some time with Glokta, Logen and Jezal and see what those bastards are up to today.<br/><br/>Can we take a second to applaud character development done at its finest? and</span>
  <span id="freeText8902219106199863123" style="display:none"><b>Guys! This book is so awesomely non-cliché I can't even..!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503701520ra/23687614.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, first let's put some context into why I loved this so much. So I'm working like crazy and barely have time to read more than 1 hour each day, so reading these in slow doses over 1 month has been such a treat.. I would come back every day eager to jump into my pajamas and spend some time with Glokta, Logen and Jezal and see what those bastards are up to today.<br><br>Can we take a second to applaud character development done at its finest? and when I say development it could be to the better, the worse or just to the batshit crazy, which I honestly haven't seen done that much before.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455403830ra/18098504.gif" width="322" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me add that this book probably contains the single most hilarious sex scene I have ever read about *slo-mo claps* <br>This book is such an amazing blend of brutal, gory, awkward, funny, dark, touching, sad, exhilarating, I wouldn't know where to start in my review.. I'll just throw this quote at you while I try to gather my thoughts.<br><i>
  <b>" 'You could not even guess at the things that I have done. Awful, evil, obscene, the telling of them alone could make you puke.' He shrugged. 'They nag at me from time to time, but I tell myself I had good reasons. The years pass, the unimaginable becomes everyday, the hideous becomes tedious, the unbearable becomes routine. I push it all into the dark corners of my mind, and it's incredible the room back there. Amazing what one can live with.' "</b>
</i><br><br>See, see?! Anyway, it may not be the best book to binge-read, but it's the best thing that happened to me during a stressful month (Petrik man, I owe you! :D), and the characters are so worth it... They all will probably be committed for intensive psychotherapy if they were real, and they do make me question my morals every time shit goes down and I cheer for those shady bastards.<br>Only one book left in the trilogy and I can't wait to see how all the craziness that happened in book 2 will unfold! Hopefully it'll take me less than a month to finish this time :P</span>
  <a data-text-id="8902219106199863123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

	<tr>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GBrqhodK2LFljY73Tui5+fQMQaa4+rk79AAiy9AyG5pqQfGWUoWebCH+zg0CHvs4k9D/MPKxFNbH9sB2eCgQIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Vg9EDowdjddramo0NMneJI2LKo8t8c8Xwa7jvlVlVUEkVF8eWdLLCi8ZKs54P5zl6leUGWe6YvryWAED/X9e+g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2355392783276518554">Joe Abercrombie was educated at Lancaster Royal Grammar School and Manchester University, where he studied psychology. He moved into television production before taking up a career as a freelance film editor. During a break between jobs he began writing <i>The Blade Itself</i> in 2002, completing it in 2004. It was published by Gollancz in 2006 and was followed by two other books in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/43644-the-first-law' rel='nofollow noopener'><i>The First Law</i> trilogy</a></span>
  <span id="freeText2355392783276518554" style="display:none">Joe Abercrombie was educated at Lancaster Royal Grammar School and Manchester University, where he studied psychology. He moved into television production before taking up a career as a freelance film editor. During a break between jobs he began writing <i>The Blade Itself</i> in 2002, completing it in 2004. It was published by Gollancz in 2006 and was followed by two other books in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43644-the-first-law" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>The First Law</i> trilogy</a>, <i>Before They Are Hanged</i> and <i>Last Argument of Kings</i>. He currently lives and works in London with his wife and daughter. In early 2008 Joe Abercrombie was one of the contributors to the BBC Worlds of Fantasy series, alongside other contributors such as Michael Moorcock, Terry Pratchett and China Mieville.</span>
